In HTML, numeric entities like `&#38;` or hexadecimal entities like `&#x26;` should be parsed where the entire `&#...;` sequence represents the ampersand's encoding. However, my current regex treats the `#` as part of the alternative list within the main non-capturing group.\n\nWait, let's trace the logic for `&#38;`. The regex engine would match the `&`. Actually, this regex requires the `&` symbol itself to be immediately followed by the `#`. While `&#38;` does start with `&`, the way the alternation is written, it seems to expect `&` to be the prefix of the entity name itself, rather than the entity being a separate token that starts with `&`. \n\nBut let's look even closer at the hexadecimal part: `#(?:39|(?:#x[\\da-fA-F]+|\\d+))`. In that case, standard assignment fails silently, but `defineProperty` actually throws a `TypeError`. This is a classic trap: the fix for one bug becomes the cause of another.\n\nWait, let me look at the test suite again. The test `should not throw strict mode errors` is specifically checking methods like `assign`, `merge`, and `defaults`. It freezes an object and then expects the assignment to happen without throwing an error. This confirms that Lodash's internal assignment logic, which eventually relies on `baseAssignValue`, must be non-destructive. It shouldn't error out if it encounters a frozen property, but it also needs to succeed when the property is shadowed on a frozen *prototype*.\n\nBut how can I distinguish between a frozen object and a frozen prototype? \n\nActually, if I look at `Object.prototype` specifically, it's quite unique. It is the root of almost all objects. If `Object.prototype` is frozen, then properties like `hasOwnProperty`, `toString`, and `constructor` become non-writable and non-configurable on that specific object. When a user tries to clone an object that has its own `hasOwnProperty` property, the cloning logic will eventually call something like `baseAssignValue(result, 'hasOwnProperty', value)`.\n\nIf `Object.prototype` is frozen, the simple assignment `object[key] = value` inside `baseAssignValue` will fail because it's trying to write to a property that is inherited and now non-writable. But if I use `Object.defineProperty`, I can force the creation of an 'own' property on the new object, which shadows the frozen prototype property. \n\nThe problem is that for a *frozen object* (not the prototype), `Object.defineProperty` on an existing property will fail if that property is non-configurable. If the property doesn't exist, it will also fail if the object is non-extensible. \n\nSo, I need a way to detect if the target object is `Object.prototype` or the global object before deciding which strategy to use. If it's a special internal object, maybe I should avoid `defineProperty`? No, that's too narrow. The bug says \"When Object.prototype (or any prototype in the prototype chain) is frozen\". This could be any prototype in the chain, not just the root.\n\nWait... if `Object.defineProperty` works for the prototype case but fails for the frozen object case, and simple assignment works for the frozen object case (silently failing) but fails for the frozen prototype case... I need a hybrid approach. \n\nActually, the most reliable way is to check if the property exists on the object itself vs. the prototype. If `hasOwnProperty.call(object, key)` is true, and the object is frozen, we should probably just try the standard assignment and ignore the error (or catch it). If `hasOwnProperty` is false, it means the property is inherited. In that case, if we want to set it, we *must* use `Object.defineProperty` to create an own property.\n\nBut there's a catch: `baseAssignValue` is used in many places. Adding a `hasOwnProperty` check and multiple `try-catch` blocks might impact performance. \n\nLet me reconsider. The test says: `var object = freeze({ 'a': undefined, 'b': function() {} }); func(object, isBindAll ? 'b' : { 'a': 1 });`. Here, the object is frozen, and we are trying to assign to property `a`. Since `a` exists on the frozen object, standard assignment `object.a = 1` fails silently. `Object.defineProperty(object, 'a', ...)` throws. The test expects no error. \n\nIn the `clone` bug, we are creating a *new* object `result = {}`. If `Object.prototype` is frozen, and we do `result.hasOwnProperty = 'foo'`, it fails. Here, `hasOwnProperty` is NOT an own property of `result`. \n\nSo the logic should be: \n1. Check if the property is an own property of the target object.\n2. If it is an own property, use standard assignment (it will fail silently if frozen, which is the desired behavior for the `assign`/`merge` tests).\n3. If it is NOT an own property (inherited from a potentially frozen prototype), use `Object.defineProperty` to create an own property.\n\nThis seems robust. It avoids the `TypeError` on frozen objects (because we only use standard assignment there) and fixes the cloning issue on frozen prototypes (because we use `defineProperty` to shadow). \n\nBefore I implement this, I need to examine the current implementation of `baseAssignValue` in `lodash.js`. I need to see if it already has any special handling for `__proto__` or if it's a very simple function. I'll read the source code around line 2604 to get the full context of how assignments are currently processed.","encrypted":null}}}}}

The `baseAssignValue` function used simple assignment (`object[key] = value`) for all properties except `__proto__`. \n\nWhen cloning an object that has a property named the same as a frozen prototype property (e.g., `hasOwnProperty`), the simple assignment fails because:\n1. In sloppy mode: The assignment fails silently (the property is not created)\n2. In strict mode: A `TypeError` is thrown\n\nThis caused `_.clone` and `_.cloneDeep` to silently drop own properties whose names collided with frozen prototype properties.\n\n### The Fix\n\nModified the `baseAssignValue` function in `/lodash/lodash.js` (lines 2604-2625) to use `Object.defineProperty` when:\n1. The property doesn't already exist as an own property on the target object\n2. `Object.defineProperty` is available\n\nThe fix works by:\n- Checking if the property already exists as an own property using `hasOwnProperty.call(object, key)`\n- If the property doesn't exist (e.g., when creating a new clone), using `Object.defineProperty` to create the property, which bypasses the frozen prototype issue\n- If the property already exists, using simple assignment (preserving existing behavior for frozen objects)\n\n### Test Results\n\n- **Original frozen prototype tests**: All pass (properties like `hasOwnProperty`, `toString`, `valueOf` are now preserved during cloning)\n- **Full test suite**: 6,807 main tests + 327 fp tests all pass (no regressions)\n- **Strict mode frozen object tests**: Pass (no change in behavior for frozen objects)\n\n### Files Modified\n\n- `/lodash/lodash.js` - Modified the `baseAssignValue` function to use `Object.defineProperty` for new properties when `defineProperty` is available and the property doesn't exist as an own property"}}}}}
